                   RECORD OF PROCEEDINGS
PETITION FOR SPECIAL LEAVE TO APPEAL (CRL.)
NO.11260/2026
[Arising out of impugned final judgment and order
dated  05-05-2026 in CRLM No. 51375/2025 passed by
the High Court of Judicature at Patna]
RAM PUKAR YADAV & ANR.              Petitioner(s)
                        VERSUS
THE STATE OF BIHAR & ANR.           Respondent(s)
IA No. 178757/2026 - EXEMPTION FROM FILING C/C OF
THE  IMPUGNED  JUDGMENT,  IA  No.  178758/2026  -
EXEMPTION FROM FILING O.T.
 
Date : 16-06-2026 This matter was called on for 
hearing today.
CORAM : HON'BLE MR. JUSTICE UJJAL BHUYAN
         HON'BLE MR. JUSTICE ARUN PALLI
[PARTIAL COURT WORKING DAYS BENCH]
For Petitioner(s) : Mr. Prabhat Ranjan Raj, AOR
                   
1

--- Page 14 ---
SLP (Crl.) No.11260/2026
For Respondent(s) : Mr. Manish Kumar, AOR
Mr. Ayush Tiwari, Adv.
Mr. Divyansh Mishra, Adv.
UPON hearing the counsel the Court made the 
following
                             O R D E R
1. We have heard learned counsel for the
petitioners and also learned counsel for
the State who has appeared on advance
notice.
2.  This  anticipatory  bail  application
arises out of a Complaint Case No. 410 of
2023 pending on the file of Learned Chief
Judicial Magistrate, Division, Madhubani,
State of Bihar. 
3. This Court has already held in SLP
(Crl.) No.16221/2015 that in a complaint
case the police has hardly any role to
play. Relevant portion of the order passed
in SLP(Crl.) No.16221/2025 reads thus:
2

--- Page 15 ---
SLP (Crl.) No.11260/2026
“7. We have noticed that there is
a serious problem in two States,
viz. the State of Bihar and State
of  Jharkhand,  respectively.  We
fail  to  understand  that  in  a
private  complaint  how  does  the
Police  involve  itself  or  is
concerned, in any manner. What was
the  basis  for  the  accused  to
express  apprehension  that  the
police would arrest them.
8. In a private complaint when
cognizance is taken and process is
issued all that the Court would do
is  to  issue  summons.  We  have
explained many times in the past
the purport of Section 87 of the
Criminal Procedure Code, 1973 (for
short, “the Cr.PC.”) The Section
87 of the Cr.PC. reads thus:-
“87. Issue of warrant
in  lieu  of,  or  in
addition to, summons.—A
3

--- Page 16 ---
SLP (Crl.) No.11260/2026
Court may, in any case
in  which  it  is
empowered by this Code
to issue a summons for
the appearance of any
person,  issue,  after
recording  its  reasons
in writing, a warrant
for his arrest—
(a) if, either before
the  issue  of  such
summons, or after the
issue of the same but
before the time fixed
for his appearance, the
Court  sees  reason  to
believe  that  he  has
absconded or will not
obey the summons;
or
(b) if at such time he
fails to appear and the
summons  is  proved  to
have been duly served
in time to admit of his
appearing in accordance
therewith  and  no
reasonable  excuse  is
offered  for  such
failure.”
9. Section 87 empowers the Court
to issue warrant in lieu of, or in
4

--- Page 17 ---
SLP (Crl.) No.11260/2026
addition  to,  summons.  However,
this power has to be exercised
only  in  two  contingencies  as
explained by the provision itself,
i.e,  (a)  and  (b),  referred  to
above, respectively.
10.  Once  the  Court  takes
cognizance and issues summons, all
that the accused has to do is to
appear before that Court and join
the proceedings. Why should the
accused  go  before  the  Sessions
Court or the High Court, as the
case  may  be,  and  pray  for
anticipatory bail? Police has no
power to arrest the accused in a
complaint case unless there is a
5

--- Page 18 ---
SLP (Crl.) No.11260/2026
non  bailable  warrant  issued  by
that Court along with the summons.
 11. We may give one another simple
illustration. Take a case wherein
on  a  private  complaint,  the
magistrate  deems  fit  to  take
cognizance under Section 200 of
the Cr.PC. but postpones the issue
of process till the conclusion of
the  magisterial  inquiry  under
Section 202 of the Cr.P.C. If a
magistrate orders a Police inquiry
under Section 202 and asks the
police  to  give  a  report,  then
whether  in  the  course  of  such
inquiry, the police can arrest the
accused. The answer is an emphatic
“NO”,  Police  has  no  powers  to
6

--- Page 19 ---
SLP (Crl.) No.11260/2026
arrest even during the course of
the inquiry under Section 202 of
the Cr.PC.”
4. That being the position, there is no
question of the petitioners being taken
into custody by the police.
5. Consequently,  the  impugned  order
dated 05.05.2026 is set aside. 
6. The  special  leave  petition  is,
accordingly, allowed.
7. Pending  application(s),  if  any,
shall stand disposed of. 
   (KAVITA PAHUJA)                (SAPNA BANSAL)
ASTT. REGISTRAR-cum-PS         COURT MASTER (NSH)
7

--- Page 20 ---

IN THE SUPREME COURT OF INDIA
CRIMINAL APPELLATE JURISDICTION
CRIMINAL APPEAL NO.       OF 2026
(Arising out of SLP(Crl.) No.11179/2026)
JATIN                       APPELLANT(S)
VERSUS
STATE OF MAHARASHTRA           RESPONDENT(S)
ORDER
1. Leave granted.
2. Heard learned counsel for the parties.
3. The appellant is in jail for seven months.
4. Admittedly,  controlled  substance  was
recovered  from  other  accused.  Prosecution
contended such controlled substance was being used
for manufacturing Narcotics.
5. Such issue may be thrashed out in the course
of Trial.
SLP(Crl.) No.11179/2026 1

--- Page 33 ---
6. We  are  aware  that  bail  granted  to  the
appellant earlier was cancelled by this Court in
Criminal Appeal No. 4614 of 2025. Since then, six
months have lapsed and investigation is complete.
There is little possibility of trial concluding in
the near future.
7. Given this situation, we are of the opinion
that further detention of the appellant is not
necessary.  Accordingly,  we  direct  that  the
appellant may be enlarged on bail subject to the
terms and conditions to the satisfaction of the
Trial Court including the condition that he shall
appear before the Trial Court on every date of
hearing; he shall not tamper with evidence or
intimidate  witnesses  and  shall  submit  his
passport, if any, before the Trial Court prior to
his release.
8. The criminal appeal stands disposed of in the
above terms.
SLP(Crl.) No.11179/2026 2

--- Page 34 ---
9. Pending application(s), if any, shall stand
disposed of.
…………………………………………………...J.
        [JOYMALYA BAGCHI]
…………………………………………………...J.
       [VIPUL M. PANCHOLI]
NEW DELHI;
17 JUNE, 2026.
SLP(Crl.) No.11179/2026 3

IN THE SUPREME COURT OF INDIA
CIVIL APPELLATE JURISDICTION
CIVIL APPEAL NO(s).         OF 2026
(arising out of SLP (C) No(s).31220/2025)
MUNIYAMMA & ANR.                                   APPELLANT(S)
                                VERSUS
MUNIRATHNAMMA & ORS.                               RESPONDENT(S)
O R D E R
1. Leave granted.
2. The appellants challenge the judgment and order dated
13.06.2025 in RSA No.1977/2021 (PAR/INJ) passed by the
High Court of Karnataka at Bengaluru.
3. As per the Office Report dated 22.05.2026, mediation
inter se the parties has been successful. We have perused
the Mediation Report dated 04.05.2026 along with the
Settlement Agreement annexed to the main paper book.
4. Learned counsel for the parties submitted that all
the disputes and differences between the parties have
been amicably resolved, and the parties have decided to
part ways on certain terms and conditions. Accordingly,
appropriate  and  necessary  orders  may  be  passed  in
accordance therewith.
5. We  appreciate  the  efforts  put  in  by  Mr.  B.C.
Thiruvengadam, learned senior counsel, who has mediated
between the parties, and also learned counsel for the
parties in helping them arrive at an amicable settlement.
1

--- Page 42 ---
6. The terms of the Settlement Agreement reads as under:
“……  1.  The  respondents  have  agreed
unconditionally  to  give  one  acre  of
agricultural land out of the Survey No.24
situated at Hithalahalli village, Kasaba
Hobli,  Sidlagatta  Taluk,  out  of  four
acres  as  described  in  item  1  of  the
plaint as well as the appeal memo and
further have agreed to give a sum of
Rupees  Twenty  Lakhs  only  to  the
Petitioners as full and final settlement
and  claim  with  respect  to  the  suit
schedule properties.
2. The Respondents shall ensure that the
Petitioners have reasonable access to the
said one acre of land, from the road
without let or hinderance to both the
parties.
3. The Respondents shall pay the sum of
Rupees Twenty lakhs within a period of
six months from the date of order of the
Hon'ble  Supreme  Court,  without  seeking
further extension of time.
4.  The  Petitioners  give  up  all  other
rights and claim with respect to the suit
schedule property and the same is final
and binding on the petitioners and their
legal heirs.
5. The 1 st Petitioner is represented by
her daughter, the 2nd petitioner who is
her power of attorney holder, copy of
which  is  enclosed  herewith  along  with
attested copy of their aadhar cards and
duly attested by their counsels. …..”
7. In view of the above, the following directions are
issued:
i) All the legal proceedings pending  inter se  the
parties, if any, shall stand closed;
ii) Decree be drawn up accordingly;
iii) It goes without saying that both the parties
2

--- Page 43 ---
will continue to abide by the terms of the Settlement
Agreement without any exception;
iv) The impugned judgment/order dated 13.06.2025 is
modified accordingly;
v) The  terms  of  the  Settlement  Agreement  are
binding upon the parties. The parties undertake to
abide by the same; and
vi) The  parties,  through  their  learned  counsel
present in the Court, have been made aware of the
consequences of breach of such terms, including the
initiation of contempt proceedings.
8. Accordingly, the present appeal stands disposed of.
9. Pending application(s), if any, shall also stand
disposed of.

ITEM NO.24               COURT NO.5               SECTION IV-B
               S U P R E M E  C O U R T  O F  I N D I A
                       RECORD OF PROCEEDINGS
SPECIAL LEAVE PETITION (CIVIL) Diary No(s). 28802/2026
[Arising out of impugned final judgment and order dated  28-01-2026
in CWP No. 35491/2025 passed by the High Court of Punjab & Haryana
at Chandigarh]
M/S KAMAL IDEAL INFRATECH PRIVATE LIMITED          Petitioner(s)
                                VERSUS
UNION OF INDIA & ORS.                              Respondent(s)
IA No. 174388/2026 - CONDONATION OF DELAY IN FILING
 
Date : 16-06-2026 This matter was called on for hearing today.
CORAM :  HON'BLE MR. JUSTICE JOYMALYA BAGCHI
         HON'BLE MR. JUSTICE VIPUL M. PANCHOLI
(PARTIAL COURT WORKING DAYS BENCH)
For Petitioner(s) :Mr. Raghavendra Pratap Singh, AOR
                   Mr. Dharmender Kumar, Adv.
                   Mr. Rajkumar, Adv.
                   Mr. Pankaj Chaudhary, Adv.
                   Mr. Mahendra Pratap Singh, Adv.
                   Mr. Ved Prakash Pandey, Adv.
                                      
For Respondent(s) : 
          UPON hearing the counsel the Court made the following
                             O R D E R
1. Delay condoned.
2. Learned counsel for the petitioner submits that the material
facts disclosing necessary ingredients for invoking Section 74 of
the Central Goods and Service Tax Act, 2017 (for short, 'the CGST
1 of 3

--- Page 56 ---
Act') has not been disclosed. There is no willful suppression of
material facts and the Input Tax Credit (ITC) claimed in the
returns filed for October 2017  has been subsequently voluntarily
reversed in the returns filed for November, 2017. It is also
contended that similar issue is pending consideration before this
Court in SLP (C) No. 33594 of 2025.
3. We have considered the show cause notice dated 08.09.2023 and
the  assessment  order  dated  07.11.2023  passed  by  the  Officer
concerned. It is patently clear from the order impugned that the
factual matrix giving rise to the show cause notice has been
elaborately discussed.  It was open to the petitioner to assail the
assessment order by way of an appeal under Section 107 of the CGST
Act. He contends that he was unaware of the order which had been
uploaded on the electronic portal. No convincing reason to overlook
the electronic communication is offered. That apart, petitioner by
his own admission was  made aware of the proceedings much earlier
in 2024 and thereafter approached the High Court belatedly in 2025.
The High Court had rightly declined to entertain the Writ Petition
as a surrogate to appellate proceedings which the petitioner had
not availed and had become time barred. Present case stands on a
different factual matter from SLP (C) No. 33594 of 2025  where the
show cause notice under Section 74 of the CGST Act had been
challenged on the ground primary facts disclosing suppression had
not been stated. In view of these facts, we are not inclined to
entertain the Special Leave Petition. 
4. The Special Leave Petition is accordingly dismissed and the
2 of 3

--- Page 57 ---
accompanying interlocutory application(s), if any, stands disposed
of.  
(KAPIL TANDON)                                (CHETNA BALOONI)
COURT MASTER (SH)                             COURT MASTER (NSH)
3 of 3

OM HARI ARORA                                      Petitioner(s)
                                VERSUS
UNION OF INDIA & ORS.                              Respondent(s)
(FOR ADMISSION 
IA No. 175513/2026 - STAY APPLICATION)
 
Date : 17-06-2026 This matter was called on for hearing today.
CORAM : 
         HON'BLE MR. JUSTICE JOYMALYA BAGCHI
         HON'BLE MR. JUSTICE VIPUL M. PANCHOLI
[PARTIAL COURT WORKING DAYS BENCH]
For Petitioner(s)  Mr. Jatin, AOR
                   Mr. R K Mishra, Adv.
                   Mr. R Satish Kumar, Adv.
                   Mr. Rahul Gulia, Adv.                   
                   
For Respondent(s) 
          UPON hearing the counsel the Court made the following
                             O R D E R
1. We have examined the Tripartite Agreement.
Though the agreement states that the loan is to be
advanced to the builder, the essential features of
a subvention arrangement namely, release of funds
on a construction linked basis or the postponement
of payment of equated monthly installment by the
borrower till the possession is handed over is
significantly absent. Therefore, the present case
is not similar to Himanshu Singh & Ors. Vs. Union
of India & Ors.[SLP(C) No. 7649 of 2023].

--- Page 74 ---
2
2. In view of the above, the writ petition is
not entertained and hereby dismissed.
3. However, it is open for the petitioner to
pursue other remedies in accordance with law.
4. Pending application(s), if any, shall stand
disposed of.
(SNEHA DAS)                              (CHETNA BALOONI)

--- Page 76 ---
2
of the five vessels. The High Court has rightly
held that the dispute fell within the ambit of

(Jurisdiction and Settlement of Maritime Claims)
Act, 2017.
4. Given this situation, direction for arrest
is unexceptionable.

secure the claim before the High Court and seek
modification of the arrest order.

approached the High Court for vacating the arrest
order on securing the maritime claim, the High
Court shall make all endeavor to dispose of the
application at the earliest.

learned  Single  Judge  would  take  a  decision
independently and in accordance with law.

disposed of.

         HON'BLE MR. JUSTICE VIPUL M. PANCHOLI
[PARTIAL COURT WORKING DAYS BENCH]

                   Mr. Sudhakar Tiwari, Adv.

                   Mr. Manoj Kumar, Adv.
                   Mr. Akshat Srivastava, AOR                     
For Respondent(s) : 
          UPON hearing the counsel the Court made the following
                             O R D E R
1. The tender process has been withdrawn in 2025.
2. The  L-1  tenderer  challenged  the  cancellation  in  a  writ
proceeding before the High Court which came to be withdrawn.
Initially,  the  petitioner  was  permitted  impleadment  in  the
proceedings. Although the cancellation had been made in 2025,
petitioner had not chosen to initiate an independent proceedings
earlier.
2. As the petitioner was neither the L-1 bidder nor any LOA had
been issued in his favour, we are of the opinion that he is unable

--- Page 128 ---
2
to make out the case of breach of any fundamental right which would
entitle him to relief under Article 132 of the Constitution of
India.
3. Accordingly, the Writ Petition stands dismissed.
4. However, the petitioner would be at liberty to participate in
accordance with law in any tender proceedings which may be floated
in future.
5. Pending applications, if any, shall stand disposed of.
